Compare unbiased conditioning and anchoring bias conditioning.
In these tests we also compare when the two methods idenitfy the actual world to see if anchoring bias conditioning is faster than unbiased conditionin.
These tests also include resources of the agents in order to see whether anchoring bias is good method as an heuristic.
First states and observables are created and then the plausibility orders of the agents.
The two agents have the same plausibility orders, but different stubbornness degrees. 

200 randomly created tests will be generated and the success percentage will be displayed in the end.
The given states are: s, x, g, r, k
The actual world is: g
The given observables are: A:{'s', 'r'}, ~A:{'x', 'g', 'k'}, B:{'s'}, ~B:{'x', 'g', 'r', 'k'}, ~E:{'s', 'x'}, E:{'g', 'r', 'k'}, D:{'x', 'k'}, ~D:{'s', 'g', 'r'}, 

The data sequence the agents received is: ~D, E, ~B, ~A, ~A, ~B, 

Unbiased agent's initial plausibility order: s:['g'], x:['s', 'k', 'g'], g:[], r:['s', 'k', 'g'], k:['g'], 
Unbiased agent's stubbornness degrees: A:1, ~A:1, B:1, ~B:1, ~E:1, E:1, D:1, ~D:1, 
Unbiased agent's initial resources: 75.08
Unbiased agent's plausibility order after receiving ~D: s:['g'], g:[], r:['s', 'g'], 
Unbiased agent's resources: 1.5016
Unbiased agent's plausibility order after receiving E: g:[], r:['g'], 
Unbiased agent's resources: 0.030032
Unbiased agent's most plausible world: r
Unbiased agent failed to identify the actual world!

Biased agent's initial plausibility order: s:['g'], x:['s', 'k', 'g'], g:[], r:['s', 'k', 'g'], k:['g'], 
Biased agent's stubbornness degrees: 
Biased agent's initial resources: 75.08
Biased agent's plausibility order after receiving ~D: r:[], 
Biased agent's resources: 1.5016
Biased agent's plausibility order after receiving E: r:[], 
Biased agent's resources: 0.030032

Biased agent's most plausible world: r
Biased agent failed to identifiy the actual world!
